After I have completed for you O Sons the book which is the ultimate science in medicine with its complement and having reached the end of it from its expositions and declarations, it appeared to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise, which is a part of practical application, that is surgery using hands.
Since surgical practice with the hand has been neglected in our region and our time: until perhaps its science perishes and its trace is completely cut off; and there remains of it nothing but small descriptions in ancient books which have been distorted by later hands, and upon which error and hesitation occur, until its intentions are obscured and its vision prolonged - It seemed to me that I should revive it with the ordering of this Treatise on surgical practice according to the way of exposition, declaration and abbreviation; and so that I may come to know the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of surgery by means of addition in their description and of their necessary preparation.
The reason why a good practitioner of this surgery with his own hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy which Galen described until he knows the structures of members and their forms, and how they are joined together or separated; and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and their numbers, and knows how they move, and of veins - both those that pulse and those at rest - and where they emerge.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that a name is great with a name, but small with a deed, and especially in the art of hand surgery.
We have indeed said this about it in the introduction to this book.
For those who are not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy, they will not be cleared of error, in which people are killed; as I myself have witnessed many among them who are trained in this science and boast of it without knowledge or experience.
What happened is because I saw a foolish physician cut a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck and he severed some arteries in her neck; thus the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead between his hands.
And I witnessed another physician who presumed to extract a stone from an aged man and the stone was large. It therefore reached him, and he extracted it with a fragment of bladder. Thus the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been called to extract it; and upon seeing the size of the stone, and considering the patient's condition, I knew that he would die.
And I witnessed another physician who was taking a fee from one of the Dukes of our land for his services; and it so happened that a black eunuch, who belonged to him, suffered a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the doctor hastened with his ignorance and bound up the fracture over the wound with plasters and tight bandages, and he did not allow any release for the injury.
Then he discharged him according to his desires. Afterwards he let him go after a few days and instructed him not to loosen the bandage; and he remained like that until an abscess formed on his leg and foot, and it resulted in his ruin.
I was called upon and hurried to release the ligament; thus tranquility ensued, and he escaped his pains.
However, the deformity had already set in firmly on his limb; I was unable to rectify it.
He consequently ceased walking due to the deformity on his limb until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who pierced an abscess filled with cancerous matter; it became ulcerated after a few days until its malignancy was magnified before its owner's eyes.
This is because when cancer is pure and comes from a melancholy humour, it ought not to be approached with the iron at all unless it is on a limb that can tolerate having its entirety cut off.
And for this reason, my sons, you must know that surgical work is divided into two branches: namely, operations which are associated with a cure; and operations where there is risk in numerous situations.
And I have already aroused you everywhere in this book to where the operation involves dread and fear.
It is necessary for you to beware of that and avoid it so that the unlearned do not find a way to speak about it and bring dishonour upon it.
Therefore take the measure with care and protection and your patients with ease and firmness; and go by a better way, leading to healing and laudable succession through God's grace; and abandon those dire diseases which are hard to cure; and remove from yourselves what makes you afraid so that hesitation does not come upon you in faith and gain.
It is indeed more conducive to your glory, and loftier in this world, and ultimately to your status.
Galen has indeed said as much in some of his admonitions. Do not treat an evil disease, lest you be called bad doctors.
I have now divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
Chapter One.
On cauterization with fire and with sharp instruments, systematic and ordered from head to toe, the shapes of the instruments and tools used for cauterization, and everything that is necessary for such operations.
Chapter Two.
On cutting and piercing, bloodletting and boils, wounds; on extracting arrows and the like; likewise ordered and systematic regarding the shapes of instruments.
Chapter Three.
On restoration and dislocations, curing twists and the like; likewise ordered from head to toe and systematic regarding the shapes of instruments.
But before recalling the operations with it, one should speak of its qualities and harms; on which constitutions it is to be used.
I say, therefore, that a discourse on the quality of cauterization and its harmful effects is an extensive, subtle matter, a science, and a hidden secret.
A multitude of wise men also spoke on it, and they disagreed among themselves; for me, a little from their discourses suffices, fearing prolixity.
I say, therefore, that cauterization universally suits all constitutions, whether with or without material; except for two constitutions, which are the hot constitution without material and the dry constitution without material.
However, they disagreed about the hot and dry constitutions with material. Some said that cauterization is beneficial for them. And others said the opposite, that cauterization is not suitable for an illness arising from heat and dryness; since the nature of fire is heat, it is unsuitable to heal a hot and dry illness with something hot and dry.
And he who said the opposite stated: cauterization benefits all hot and dry illnesses that occur in human bodies; for when you compare a human body and its humors to the constitution of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I say, from his discourse: because experience has already proven this to me several times.
However, one should not attempt it unless he is already proven and practiced in the last chapter's exercise on cauterization practice, and has knowledge of the variety of human constitutions and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, their causes, incidents, and duration.
Among other body types, there is no need for concern; especially with cold and damp illnesses. For all physicians have indeed agreed upon them; and they do not dissent on the usefulness of cauterization for these.
And know, my children, that from the secret of cure by cauterization with fire, its goodness is superior to that of cauterization with burning medicine; for fire is simple, whose action does not reach unless to the member which is cauterized: and it harms no other member joined to it, save for a small injury.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which extends from the members: and perhaps it causes to happen in the member a difficult-to-heal illness, and perhaps it kills.
But fire, because of its subtlety and goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless it is excessive.
It has already become apparent to us through experimentation, due to the length of our service and study with this art, and our standing on the truth of things: and I am absolved from the length of my speech because of that.
And if it were not for the fact that it is not permitted to reveal in this my book the hidden secret of fire and the quality of its operation in bodies by means of expelling illnesses, which it demonstrates with philosophical reasoning that would sharpen your minds.
And know, my children, that they themselves disagree on the timing, at which it is appropriate to perform a cauterization, and place greater value on the proper time with truthful reasoning.
And I say that a cauterization is appropriate at any time: for this reason, that the harm of an accident due to timing is submerged in the benefit which is drawn with cauterization. And especially if cauterization is done because of pains arising from necessary injuries, strong and severe ones that do not tolerate delay: for this reason, there is a fear that the worse harm will occur rather than a minor injury caused by delaying treatment.
And do not let it occur to your minds, o sons, that which only the laymen and foolish physicians do not consider, namely that for illnesses which are healed by cauterization there is not always a relapse: they regard this as its consequence but it is not so; for cauterization serves no purpose other than in place of medicine, altering the body's constitution and drying up the moist humours which cause pain.
However, cauterization surpasses medicine because of the speed with which it heals, and its powerful mode of operation, and the intensity of its control; and it is possible that there may be a relapse after some time according to the patient's constitution, and the location of their illness, as well as its severity, and what has been prepared in their body from an excess of humours within them, or what has reached them through acquisition from food, or similar causes unless they fall ill with something which requires cauterization.
A subtle illness in a limb which is caused by an excess of humours and moistness, such as the cauterization of a tooth due to pain, or similar cases may not relapse. But this occurs in few cases.
However, the layman's saying that cauterization is medicine's last resort is correct, but not as they intend it; for they believe there to be no cure which can match medicine or any other treatment once cauterization has been applied.
However, the reality is the opposite of that, and the intent, which is that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, it is not so unless when we apply methods of treatment for some illnesses and those medications are ineffective; then we perform cauterization as a last resort, and it works: from this comes the saying, 'cauterization is the last resort in medicine,' but not according to the intent that the general public and many foolish doctors understand.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold and the loftiness of its substance; and they said that the site of cauterization does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely true, for I have already proven it and found that it does not do so in some bodies without others.
And cauterization with gold is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you heat the cautery over fire made from gold, it does not indicate to you when it has been heated according to the amount that you desire due to the redness of the gold; and when it quickly becomes cold, and if you add more ignition to it, it melts in the fire and turns into flakes.
That is why the artisan falls short with it for the task; and because of this, cauterization with iron among us is faster and more immediate in terms of preparedness to perform the procedure.
And I indeed have already arranged this chapter on cauterization according to topics, and I have arranged it from head to toe so as to facilitate the search for whoever wants something from it.
Head, second degree.
This cauterization is applicable to the dominance of moisture and coldness over the brain: which are two causes of headaches, and the multitude of fluid flowing from the head towards the eyes and ears, and the abundance of sleepiness, toothache, and throat pain: and universally for all illnesses that occur due to coldness, such as paralysis, fainting, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
The method of cauterization is to instruct the patient to first evacuate their head with a cleansing, dissolving medicine for three nights or four, according to how strong the patient is, and his age, and what he is used to.
Then instruct him to scrape his head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands in the shape of a square so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that place with the cautery.
Then fire the olive oil cautery, which is of this form.
Then place it over the marked spot with the cautery, pressing down in a manner that your hand becomes constricted gradually, and you roll it around. Then remove your hand quickly, and look at the spot.
If you see that an amount of bone the size of a chickpea or the size of a stinging nettle has already been burnt away, then lift your hand up. If not, repeat with your hand using the same iron, or another one if this one has cooled down: until you see the bones I mentioned to you.
Then take some salt, dissolve it in water, soak the dressing in it, and place it on the wound: leave it for three days.
Then place the soaked dressing on butter, and leave it on until the fire-wound scab is destroyed. Then treat it with the four-herb ointment until it is healed.
They already said that the more a wound remains open, the more it discharges pus: which is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said to cauterise the skin down to the bone: and hold the cautery there until something thick from the bone burns.
Then scrape after what has been burnt of the bone, then treat it.
And others say that one must reach with the cautery to the end, until it leaves an impression on the bone like a seal stamp: or a tool that women use for putting small letters; and they believe that vapours of the head will escape from this place, and the wound should be left open for long time.
Then treat it until it becomes solid.
But to me, these two types of cauterisation seem suitable only for some people with a tendency towards fear.
And letting it be, in my view, is better for their health.
For the head becomes weak due to the dissolution of its inherent continuity; as we have witnessed in other body parts; especially when by nature an ill person's head is frail; and I find the first type of cauterization safer and better, so I use it; therefore work with it for healing.
Head: Three.
When a prolonged chronic pain occurs all over the head; and it is treated with herbs, leeches, clysters, oils, and embrocations. And especially if it has already been cauterized once with the type we described and none of those treatments help; then consider this. For if the patient's head is of a strong build by nature and not weak, but feels excessive cold; then cauterize it with another type of cautery underneath to a lesser degree. Then cauterize it over the entire horn of its head with a cautery that does not penetrate through the skin and reveals an amount of bone as we described. And cauterize it with one type on the occipital bone of its head, in a place called vas, which is where the windpipe is located; and raise your hand here, and do not reveal the bone. For the patient feels a severe pain from it, different from the pains of all other types of cauterization of the head.
And I will call this the Cautery of its Place; and it should be a cautery that is finer than the one used to cauterize the horns of the head and its occipital bone when cauterizing its centre.
Chapter Four.
When there is pain and swelling on the head, or when the pain extends to the eye, and it is evacuated with cleansing medicines for the head, and the rest of the treatment that I mentioned in the sections on diseases does not help completely; then cauterization of this condition should be done in two ways: either by cauterization with burning medicine, or with an iron.
Cauterization with burning medicine is done by taking one alum, scraping it and cutting off its ends on both sides. Then cut the painful spot at an opportune time with a broad lancet until there is made in it beneath the skin a place into which the tooth can be fitted.
Insert it into the skin so that it is hidden; then bind over it with a compress of suitable tightness and leave it for fifteen hours; then release it, take out the tooth, and allow the wound to rest two or three days. Afterwards, apply to it, an ointment soaked in butter until the spot forms pus; afterwards treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do it with some burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on caustic medicines.
Cauterization with an iron is done in this way. With the cautery fire whose form is thus:
The clavicle is so named because the shape of its head is like that of a nail, which has a certain curvature, and in its middle there is a small eminence.
Then place it on the site and hold your hand; you roll the blade gradually with speed, and let the amount that is cauterized by its thickness be like half of (the skin). Raise your hand so that the artery below is not cauterized, for a bleeding will occur.
Then soak a compress in salt water and place it on the site for three days; then apply a compress with butter; afterward treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this temple with the second knife-like extremity of the Cauterium. And beware of cutting an artery in this temple, not one that is old.
On the method of cauterizing an old temple.
When treating a temple with what we have said from the previous treatment and what we mentioned in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment does not work; and you see that it is insufficient for the illness what we previously stated about cauterizing with medicine or cauterization by fire, then it is necessary to use the knife-like Cauterium until it whitens after you mark on the site of pain a line whose length is half a finger, or something like that; and remove your hand once, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, you must be careful to avoid the continuation of the jawbone, which moves during chewing, lest the side or the nerve that moves it be burned, causing a spasm.
And remain above the cost, and take care of the arterial blood flow, which has been cut off. Indeed, its cutting off is feared, and especially by him who does not know what he is doing and is neither studious nor experienced; and he abandons the operation with him first.
And I will come with the recollection of the treatment for accidental arterial blood flow according to its manner and in this book's place.
If you see from the illness that it is not sufficient for him with this cautery, and you see the patient's body tolerate the cautery in the middle of the head, as we described, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we said in the chapter on extracting an artery with a cautery having two knives. This cautery is better and more effective.
On the method of cauterizing for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with solutions and other treatments we mentioned before, but the pain does not go away, then cautery by fire; this is called a puncture whose form is as follows...
Then puncture with it all around the ear as it revolves; or all around each one if pain is present in both simultaneously. And extend yourself with the cautery from the root of the ear for a short while, after you have marked the places with the encaustrum; and let the amount of cauterization be ten points in every ear, and so on.
Then care for the places until they heal.
The way of cauterization in Torture.
Chapter 7.
The torture which is cured by means of cautery is only of that kind which happens through the phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
And turn aside the cautery from that kind which happens through drying out and a nerve spasm.
When you treat this kind of torture with ipecacuanha, emetics, and gargles but your treatment does not work then it is necessary that you cauterize the sick person three times; once at the root of the ear, and a second time just below the tympanum, and thirdly where the two lips meet.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the sick part. Because softening does not occur unless it happens on that part which appears to be healthy.
And the form of the cautery is such that you cauterize with a cautery the upper end of the ear under the horn of the head slightly, and another on the tympanum; whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And leave your hand with the cautery until half of its thickness has been burnt.
This is the form of a cautery, and it is made from a lancet with the aforementioned shape; however, it should not be too delicate, as you can see, and there must be a little superfluous thickness to the blade.
Then treat the wound as described previously until it is healed.
The method of cauterising an old stroke.
When an old stroke is treated and you have taken care of it as described but your treatment does not work, and the patient has no fever, then cauterise them with four cauteries on each corner of their head, one in the middle of the head, and another at the back of the head, as explained previously; apply cautery according to the method outlined above.
The stomach bone is also treated with cautery, which is generally the final step in treatment.
Afterwards it should be treated as previously described.
Chapter 9.
The patient must first be given fresh drinks and pills to cleanse the brain.
Next, shave the patient's head completely and apply to their occipital bone a plaster of mustard seed as described in the section on plasters; repeat this several times.
This is the method of cautery; apply it as previously described with the same order.
If they heal through this method, then that is good. If not, then make three cauterizations on the back of their head, which are descending from the top of the head down to the bottom part of the eye; and leave a finger's width between each cautery.
Then treat the cauterization, along with what has preceded it.
If however you wish to add more and the patient is able to tolerate it: then make a cauterization on the middle of the area. If you wish to add more, then cauterize it above two corners.
Then treat it until it is healed; let the cauterization be anointed with oil according to the form which has been described before.
A paragraph on the method of cauterization for paralysis and softening.
Chapter 10.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with hyssop, and with what we have said.
Then shave the patient's head; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery on the middle of their head, and a cautery above each corner of their head, and a cautery behind them, and three over the vertebrae of their neck.
If however you need to soften the patient's body with more cauteries, and they are able to tolerate it, and their illness is severe: then cauterize them with four cauteries over the vertebrae of their back, and the last one with a cautery until most of its surface blisters out of their skin, and lift your hand upwards. Then treat it until it is healed; anoint the cauterization with oil thusly.
The method of cauterization for epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless their epilepsy is caused by phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you first clean their brain with hyoscyamus, and with the rest of the treatment we described in the division: when the patient is strong or tolerant to accepting medicines.
But if it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then give them mouthwashes and chewing cleansers for the brain, before that on many days with good food.
Then shave his head, then cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, as preceded in the method: and another on his occipital bone, and over every horn of his head. If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize them with the cauteries that I mentioned for one having paralysis, and a softening of the body over the cervical vertebrae and dorsal vertebrae: and let the cautery be olive oil according to the method which preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then place a fine cautery, according to this method.
The method of cauterization for melancholia.
When the cause of melancholia is corrupted moistures, and thick phlegm, then cauterize them with the cauteries that we mentioned for one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholia is an excess of black bile towards melancholia, and the patient's body is moist, then give them to drink what cleanses their brain, as preceded in the division: then shave the patient's head, and afterwards make a decently made linen cap like a circle.
Then place it on the middle of the head: and let the patient sit square and be held from every part.
Then present the ointment. And it is more worthy from old egg butter. And warm it over the fire with tempered heat to the extent that a finger could bear when inserted into it. Then evacuate it onto the middle of their head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do this for the patient once every week with the rest of their good regimen until they are healed.
Or if you wish, cauterise it by making many small holes in it, except for what you hold with your hand holding the cauterising iron: and let [the patient] be fasting.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place over it a poultice soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
A way of cauterising that descends to the eye in water.
Chapter 13.
When you ascertain that water is coming from the eye through the signs I mentioned above, then begin and make the patient drink with something that will clean their head.
And protect them from all moisture, and make them sit in the bath, fasting for a few days.
Then instruct them to shave their head, and cauterise it on the middle of their head. Then cauterize it over the two temples with two cauteries if there is an onset of watery discharge from both eyes simultaneously, or from one side if there is watery discharge from one eye; and cut through all veins and arteries that are under the skin with the cautery; and let the cauteries be as long as the width of the temples: and beware of a flow of blood.
If you see anything coming out of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with wisdom regarding the extraction and cutting of arteries, and caution against a flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two extremely hot cauteries.
The method of cauterizing for excessive weeping.
When the tears of the eyes are old and persistent, and they appear over veins and arteries that are visible on the exterior of the head, it is confirmed that this is due to an excess of cold and phlegmatic humours; then cauterize with a single cautery as I have described for the onset of watery discharge, with one cautery in the middle of the head, two cauteries over the temples, and two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if you require additional treatment, then cauterize it on every side of the eye with caution, at the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
The method of cauterizing for nasal odour.
When you treat it with what we have described for the division of treatments, and treatment is not forthcoming; then proceed swiftly, and give him a decoction made from crushed garlic in broth three times at night: thereafter shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium-sized searing iron heated with oil. Then cauterize it with two clavicle-shaped cauteries, above the eyebrows slightly beneath the hairline.
And guard against the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the shape of the clavicle cautery.
On the method of cauterizing a softened eyelid.
When the eyelid of an eye softens due to disease or moisture, then you should cauterize the softened part with one cautery, using this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the eyebrows slightly with two cauteries on each side; let them extend beyond the temples by a little bit and make every cautery of the same length as the eyelid; do not remove your hand holding the cautery until one-third of the eyelid has been burned.
On the method of cauterizing an eyelid with reversed eyelashes that irritate the eye.
The cautery in this case is of two kinds; either a fire-cautery or a caustic-medicine cautery.
For the fire-cautery, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his hair if he is one of those who cleanses himself by shaving until it grows out and becomes even in length. If, however, they irritate him at the root, then bind his eyes with a cloth so that they do not move until new eyelashes grow in their place.
When they are born and equalized, then place the patient's head in your lap; next, mark above the eyelids of his eyes with cautery, a mark that is shaped like a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the eyelashes.
Then place over the eye a poultice soaked in egg white; or use a mucilage of psyllium.
Then apply fire with the following instrument.
Then cauterize gradually over the shape you marked with many touches of the iron, until the skin surface which appears just like a myrtle leaf is completely burned away.
And you will know your work is healthy when you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting, and the eyelashes rising at the wound of the eye.
Therefore lift your hand then; and let him go after three days.
Then place over the patient a poultice with butter until the scar is removed. Then treat him with an ointment until he is healed.
If any of the eyelashes grow back after this time and the eyelid becomes soft again; then repeat the cautery on that spot as you did at first.
However if the eyelashes are on the lower lid; then cauterize it until it is lifted to its normal place and equalized so that the lashes do not poke the eye.
Advise the patient to leave the hairs [after an operation], until they grow back and become even. Make a piece of cloth in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Take an ounce of known soap and the same amount of un-soaked lime; then grind them together well, and do this quickly so that it doesn't get cold. Then spread some of it on the piece of paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over one or both eyelids. Place a soaked poultice, dipped in egg white, under the eye; and let the patient's head rest on your lap.
Put your index finger on the medicine and press it gently. And move your finger whenever the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine; for its sting is like fire.
While you persist with this which the patient finds stinging, then stop applying the medicine and move it away with your finger. When the stinging sensation subsides, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
Then observe if you see the eyelid swelling like it does when exposed to fire or cut; and if not, then repeat on it some medicine in an area where the medicine hasn't yet been applied and isn't discoloured, until your procedure is even and the eye contracts.
Then place on it a poultice with butter until the burnt skin is removed. Treat it then with diaphanicon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And during the procedure, you must take care to protect the patient's last barrier [i.e., eye], lest any of the medicine falls into it.
If the eyelid softens after a few days and something irritates the eye from the eyelashes, then repeat the medicine on that place which is softened by its own eyelid, as you did initially. Treat it until it is healed.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you should be aware that human eyes vary in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be thus: the path of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a tear duct fistula with what we said in the divisions of ailments, and your treatment does not bear fruit, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap and have an assistant hold their head between their hands so that it cannot move or be shaken.
Next, place a sponge soaked in alum, or in psyllium mucilage on their eye; then take up the cautery with this shape.
It should be hollow like the shape of an eagle-feather quill at one end, with which the cautery is done; and if you want it to penetrate all the way through to the other end, or upwards, then temper it thus.
Indeed this bowl is better for your purpose.
Next squeeze the abscess, if it is open, and extract its foul matter, then dry it out; but if it isn't open, then you must open it, and extract its puss.
Then place over it the hot cautery iron.
And hold your hand for a moment over the cautery iron from beyond the eye, towards the nose, so that you don't miss with your hand nor disturb the patient; then place the hot iron on the eye's fat and destroy it.
If therefore you make an incision with your cautery iron right down to the bone then all will be well. And if not then repeat the cautery once or twice as you need; and remove the iron after three days.
Then place on it a poultice with butter and care for it with drying ointment until it is healed.
But if after forty days it is not healed then place on it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone shows; and shave it according to what came before in this chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for abscesses which certain ancients have described. Note the position of the abscess and find it; then place into its crack a thin rod, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is thus: [shape follows]. And pour into it a drachma-sized quantity of molten lead; and hold your hand with the cannula securely, so that the patient doesn't move at all, lest the melted lead run or reach his eye.
You should place a poultice infused in egg white over the patient's eye, or in water.
For lead burns the area of the fistula, and heals it with a wondrous cure.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, it is good. And if not, it is necessary to administer a nasal passage, and redirect the fistula towards the path of the nose, according to what will come to its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing fissures on the lips.
Fissures often occur on the lips, which are called cracks, especially on the lips of children.
When you treat these fissures as we have said in the section on illnesses, and it does not provide a cure, then apply a small cautery knife with fire, according to this form.
And let it be hollowed out like the sharpness of the knife.
Then place this ignited [knife] swiftly into the very fissures until you reach the depth of the cracks with the cautery.
Then treat it with a caustic [ointment], until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing an oral fistula.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gums or on the palate or at the roots of teeth: it then causes pus and breaks open; later, it heals over, but still runs with pus, thus forming a fistula; you treat this, yet no cure takes place, so you must apply a cautery ignited according to its size such that it fits within the fistula. Insert the heated iron into the hole of the fistula and hold your hand there until the hot metal reaches its deepest point and end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said about treatment until it is cured.
So if the pus is drained and heals, it will be good. And if it does not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what comes at its head.
On how to cauterize in gingivitis and softened teeth.
When the gums are softened due to humidity and the teeth move and you treat it with medicine but it does not help, then place the patient's head on your lap.
Then use the fire cautery whose form will come later so that you place the cannula over the tooth and quickly insert into it the heated cauterium: and hold your hand a moment until the patient feels the heat of the fire has now reached the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cautery several times according to what you want.
Then let the patient fill their mouth with saltwater solution and hold it for an hour before spitting it out.
For the loose tooth is made firm, the softened gum tightened and dried up, and the corrupted humidity healed.
On how to cauterize for toothache.
When toothache is caused by coldness, either there is actual cold or worms, and treatment with medicine does not help, then cauterization on the tooth itself is performed in two ways: either cautery with butter or cautery with fire.
The cautery with butter involves taking fresh butter and boiling it in an iron spoon or a small pot. Next, take a woolen cloth and wrap it around the end of a stick or probe. Then immerse the cloth in the boiling butter and quickly place it on the painful tooth, holding it there until it cools. Repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, you can also dip the wool or cloth in cold butter and place it on the aching tooth, then put a heated iron on top of it until the heat reaches deep into the cavity of the tooth.
The cautery with fire involves using an iron or brass pipe. If the pipe has a thick wall, this prevents the sharp heat from reaching the patient's bone.
Next, apply the cautery with fire to the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery cools down.
Repeat this procedure several times; the pain will be removed either that same day or on another day.
The patient should fill their mouth with good butter after the cautery mark and hold it there for an hour before spitting it out.
And this is the form of cautery.
Scorch with whatever end you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
On the method of cauterizing with hot irons.
When hot irons are affected by phlegm and cold dampness, and do not respond to treatment with medicines, and you wish to rapidly facilitate their resolution: then use a concave cautery of this shape.
Which has two tight ends so that the smoke escapes from one end of the cautery: and place it alight on top of the swelling once, and a second time if you need to, until you reach the bottom of the swelling.
But if the swelling is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the swelling.
Then leave it for three days, and apply to it lard infused with vinegar until that which was burned by the fire is removed.
Then treat it with tooth-powder ointment until the form of the cannula is restored.
On the method of cauterizing with hoarseness of voice, and tightness of breathing.
When dampness is affecting the bronchial tubes, and especially when it comes with a cold constitution, then the patient must first be cleared out by means of liquefying medicines.
Then scorch it at night close to the base of the throat in a hollow place: and be careful not to reach with the cautery into the throat itself or anywhere on the skin except that spot.
Then cauterize it with another cautery near the neck joint at the last of his vertebrae ending here; and let this be a claw-shaped cautery according to the method, which preceded earlier.
Then treat it with what has been done before until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for lung disease and cough.
When cough and lung disease are due to cold humours, and the patient has no fever or consumption, nor an old illness: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the collar-bone in hollow places, gentle, empty ones. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples; and let this be a pipe-shaped cautery according to the form which preceded earlier.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by pricking with a cautery called 'The Point', whose form preceded earlier for piercing ear pain: and let the points be from thirty up to almost forty in number.
Then treat it with what has been done before until it is healed.
And now let this be a three-branched cautery according to the following form. Why is cauterization lightened with it when you do three cauteries together as one?
Chapter 27.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated due to moisture, and it does not return to its place at once, until it gets used to returning, then it is dislocated by a slight motion which happens as we have already shown; then you ought to reduce the dislocation first of all. Then the patient should lie down on their back or on their healthy side. Then lift the skin that is inside the armpit upwards with your left hand's fingers: and if the joint is dislocated towards the inside.
Then have a cauterizer over fire with two sticks. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the shape of the cauterization will appear with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three sticks, which results in a shape of six cauteries: and the thinness of the sticks must be considered.
And this is the form of a three-stick cautery.
And sometimes one more is added to this method, which results in eight cauteries.
Then place crushed leeks with salt on the cautery. Then ensure that the patient remains calm so as not to move their limb until they are comforted.
And if the dislocation is upwards, which rarely happens, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a key-like cautery or multiple punctures.
For the joint is strengthened, moisture removed, and the patient heals.
On cauterizing the stomach:
When there are excessive cold and moisture in the stomach, failing to remove it from its constitution, with catarrh forming frequently despite continued treatment, one must place the patient supine on their back with legs and arms extended. Then cauterize with three cauterizations: one thumb-sized sub-conchoidal chest cautery, a clavicle cautery, and two additional cauteries on either side of the single one below, until the arrangement forms a triangular shape. And space them apart so they do not join when forming pus.
The depth of the cautery should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
The arrangement of the cauteries should follow this form without addition, and if you wish to cauterize with a large one in the center of the stomach following this form: use a cautery instrument shaped like a circle as such.
Cauterize the stomach by applying this frightening cautery after marking it with a hot iron in the spot and size you desire; then cauterize that mark, followed by treatment as before until healed.
On cauterizing a cold spleen:
When there is pain in the spleen due to cold and moisture, or thick wind, until it leaves its natural constitution by excessive discharge, and the patient is treated with what we have said above without improvement; one must place them supine on their neck, then mark with a hot iron three cauterizations like this shape, and of equal size below the spleen from the hypocondria where the tip of the elbow reaches. The space between each should be the width of a finger, and the length of the cautery that of an upright body; do not press heavily with the cautery.
And let its quantity be such that it is burned due to the thickness of the skin; the quantity should be half of what was added, and the patient must stand on their own feet.
If the patient is not standing, then let them lie down with their legs already extended and arms raised.
This is the shape of the caustic/cauterizing iron.
And indeed it is possible for you to use these caustic irons like a surgical knife when you have skill and caution in the art.
And take care not to proceed too far in the cauterization and burn through all the thickness of the skin, for it will thereby burn the entire body as well, and reach the intestines; since the skin there is thin, know this.
On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When it happens and you wish to know whether the abscess is in the liver's flesh or in its membrane, then if it is in the liver's flesh, it afflicts the patient with a weighty pain without sharpness; but if it is in the liver's membrane, there is pain along with severe acuteness: and now you see that its treatment has tired out his doctors.
It is necessary, therefore, for the patient to lie down on their neck/nape. Then sketch the place of the abscess with a red-hot cautery; then take up the fiery iron, which resembles a rod. And this is its shape/form. And cauterize it with one cautery until the entire skin is burnt and reaches the bone, until all pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment of discharging [pus], until it is healed.
And one need not use this type of cautery unless they have an extended study in the art of medicine, and these illnesses pass through their hands with some experience; then indeed will they dare to perform such operations.
But as for dismissing it, in my view, it is better.
[Section title] On the method of cauterizing in cases of pleurisy.
The ancients said that the root of Aristolochia (birthwort) should be used as a cold cautery for pleurisy in this way. And it is necessary that you take from the dry roots of Aristolochia (birthwort), one longer root which can be found inside, and this should be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil; and light it on fire over the flame. Then cauterize with one cautery where it is between the fork of the collarbone and clavicle (furcula), and two small cauteries somewhat sloping downwards towards the side that lies under the jaw.
And two more cauteries where it is between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping towards the back somewhat; another on the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And three more from behind: one where it is between the two scapulae; and two on either side of the chest, with the lower cautery lying between the two scapulae.
You should not squeeze your hand with the cauterization iron; instead, it must be held in a way that allows you to smell the patient's skin clearly.
Some ancient authorities have stated that there are individuals who use an iron cautery similar to a radius; they ignite it and insert it into the space between the ribs until they reach the abscess with the hot iron, and pus emerges as we described for liver abscesses.
But this procedure of puncturing with the cautery carries a risk that either the patient will die immediately or develop a fistula at the site which cannot be cured.
On cauterizing the head of the spleen: Chapter 32.
When you treat a spleen disorder as we have described under the section on diseases of the spleen and your treatment is not effective, then cautery can be employed in three different ways which are all correct.
One method is to make three or four cauterizations by drawing a line along the length of the spleen in the same shape as the cautery marks for the liver described earlier.
The size of each individual cauterization should be that of a finger's breadth or more/less than this depending on the particular case.
The method of carrying out the procedure should be as we described for liver cautery: evenly spaced out.
Do not squeeze the patient's hand with the cautery iron; instead, let him lie on his back with you at his side.
Another method of cautery is to ignite a two-pronged iron which we described in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; raise up the skin that lies directly over the spleen where the patient's left elbow reaches when extended; and elevate it sufficiently so that you stretch the skin across his body so that the prongs fall along his length.
Then insert two very hot sticks until you pierce the skin from the other side; then withdraw the cautery instrument; thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery instrument having three prongs.
Then treat the cautery instrument after you remove it, letting it discharge pus for many days; for it is more effective than all that has gone before in terms of treatment.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of dropsy.
The cautery instrument must not fall on the dropsy unless it is properly covered with an asclit.
When you treat a case of dropsy with the methods of treatment that we have described above, and it does not respond to treatment, then it is necessary for you to cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, one cautery on the stomach, another on the liver, one on the spleen, two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, one straight over the chest, and another straight over the stomach; and let the depth of the cauteries be approximately equal to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery instrument open so that it discharges pus over a long period of time.
And you will not discharge the patient from treatment after the cautery with it: for which two intentions must be joined to it; and healing will come speedily, by God's help.
The form of the cautery instrument with which you cauterize the belly should be a nail according to what has gone before in its shape; and that of the one with which you cauterize the back should be olive-shaped, according as its previous shape was.
On the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When blisters form on the dropsy patient and fill with yellow fluid, you must cauterize above the back of the foot at night, in the place which is between the auricular and ring finger; raise your hand holding the cautery, and do not twist it; then lift your hand, and do not repeat it at all.
The yellow fluid will flow out, and the cautery should be like this shape.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with a knife-shaped end; and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other below that, about midway down the leg; and over the entire hip, two cauteries; and leave the open cautery untreated for a long time: so that some water flows out of it; then treat it with the rest which we have said.

And if you see excessive moisture and the patient can tolerate it, then cauterize it with a large cautery on a comb, and use the cautery on all of that area; perhaps you may also add two small cauteries near the stomach.
For it is a successful treatment whose aid does not go astray.

And if you think that their stomach is chilled and their food is not being digested, and you see their face breaking out in spots, then cauterize them with a large cautery on the stomach as previously described; also cauterize over their liver, and another over their spleen, with a nail-like cautery; leave the open cautery for some time; then treat it until they are healed.

On the method of cauterizing fistula-in-ano.
Chapter 38.
When the patient does not obey treatment by incision and operation as we have described in its place, and is terrified of it, perhaps he will be healed with a cautery.
When therefore it happens to someone that fistula becomes old, and is neglected, pus runs from it, and corrupted moisture. It is therefore appropriate that you should examine it with a thin probe. Then ascertain the depth of it by means of the probe.
Then light a cautery which is similar in size (to the fistula). Then introduce yourself, when it is lit, into the fistula, and that part which the probe entered.
And repeat upon it the cautery, until they burn all those corrupted parts, once or twice or three times, according to the necessity of your situation.

On the method of cauterising kidneys.
When there is pain in the kidneys due to cold or thick windiness, and it diminishes because of that weak body, then you should cauterise them over almethenem above the kidneys themselves, with a clavicle cautery on each kidney, which has been previously mentioned.

On the method of cauterising the bladder.
When there is weakness and softening in the bladder due to cold and moisture, until the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterise it at the lower part of the suminis above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, with a right sumin cautery on one side, and another on its left; and let the length of this lateral cauterisation be equal to the size of the thumb's knot; and cauterise it with a lower back cautery, or two if needed: and let it be according to the previously mentioned clavicle cautery.
The method for cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, and it is prevented from becoming pregnant, and her menses are corrupted, and their onset is delayed, and she experiences pain at their arrival, then she ought to be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with one cautery below the back over the alcatim, or two: and let the cautery be a clavicle.
The method for cauterizing the anus during dislocation.
When the moisture of the mucous membrane spills into the hollow of the anus, and becomes a cause of its exiting from its place: and its sign is that one leg extends beyond the other when they are compared to each other: and the site of dislocation will be found in it as empty.
One ought therefore to cauterize the patient above the anus's hollow with a similar circular cautery: after you mark with encausticum around the hollow as it turns: and so that the hollow itself falls into the middle of the circle.
If you do not have this cautery available, then cauterize it with three cauteries, using a large olive-oil cautery: and let the cautery's depth be according to the thickness of all the skin.
Then treat it until it heals.
The method of cauterization for sciatica.
When there is pain in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and dampness: and if treating the patient with what we have said earlier does not help and the condition persists, then it is necessary to rid the patient of gross humours with fetid pills or artificial pills and similar things. Then cauterize him/her.
And the method of cauterization on it is according to two methods: either a cauterizing agent with adhering medicines or a cauterizing iron with fire.
A cauterizing iron with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is that the cauterizing irons are placed over the hip joint in three triangular shapes, according to this form: [drawing not included] And make them of good or bad depth. And let the space between each cauterization be the size of a fingertip, and let it be an olive-oil cauterization.
Sometimes there is also a cauterization in the middle, right on top of the hip joint. Because there are four cauterizations.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose shape previously appeared in the cauterization for hip dislocation, make it so that the circle contains the entire hip.
And burn away all of the thickness of the skin.
This is the method of cauterization for sciatica when the pain is attached to the hip itself and does not extend down into the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauterizations over the hip, over the place where the patient indicates pain is felt, and with your own cautery over the shinbone four fingers away from the outer side: and let the cauterization be done with a knife.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends near the toes, then cauterize it where they indicate with a single-point, three-point, four-point or multi-point cautery, as needed.
And if they indicate pain beneath the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with a single knife-point cautery.
And be careful in all your cautery procedures not to press down hard enough with the cautery that you burn nerves or a large artery, and thereby cause harm to the patient through severe damage or contraction.
And I myself have seen one and another among those who cauterized over the shinbone and pressed too hard in their cautery procedure, and the leg became swollen until the swelling reached the foot, and it ruptured entirely, and the entire foot was destroyed: then there occurred an abdominal hernia, and death soon after.
If the pain is in two places at once, cauterize each one according to this method.
And some wise men have said about the cautery of the shoulder that this is its method. Make a similar iron cup with a diameter of half a palm's width: and let it be at its opening the thickness of a finger's core or less by a little bit: and inside this cup let there be another third cup.
And there should be the space equivalent to that between every finger according to the quantity of the knuckle of the thumb; and they must be open on both sides; and their height ought to be that of a knot, or two knots; and make for them handles out of iron, decently fitted into the scoops.
Then it is held in the fire until it glows red and throws sparks; then place it on a jar of vinegar with the affected limb resting weakly on the healthy side. Scorch him therefore with three round cauteries at one sitting.
Then leave it alone for three days. Afterwards plaster with butter; and leave the wound open many days. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasis says of this kind of cautery, my sons, we have made little use because of the fearsome look of it; and also because there are few whom we find will await its application.
Nevertheless it is among the good cauterizations for him who suffers it; and he will find its place useful.
But if the cautery is to be used with medicinals then you should make two scoops having a perforated band which descends into the hinge of its door from brass or iron, as long as the wall; and their height ought to be that of two knots, or like themselves.
And there should be the space equivalent to that between each other according to the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and they must be open below and above; and it is such as will contain one another, according to this shape.
Then place it on an anchor jar, with the patient lying on their healthy side. And press your hand firmly over the anchor jar. Then pour between the two circles some hot water, heated with fire for a while, and keep it there for a time equivalent to an hour; let the patient bear its bite and burning, for they find its bite like that of fire until the biting ceases.
Then raise your hand with the instrument, and wipe away all hot water from the anchor with fresh water; then leave it for three days.
And place butter over it until the burning blackness is removed; then leave it for a few days, and there will be pus coming out of it. For this is the final part of the treatment.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg: make for them a statue containing water where it is affected by the pain, just as you did for the anchor jar equally.
And this is how hot water should be used; I have already written it down in the book of pharmaceutical corrections. Take equal parts of alkali and unslaked lime; grind both, then place them in a new pot with its lower part pierced by one small hole according to the size that would fit a radius bone inside it: place under the bottom of this pot another worn-out pot: pour over the alkali and lime fresh water until they are submerged by an inch. After which you press it firmly with your hand; leave the pots as such until cold water comes out from the lower part of the worn-out jar.
Then pour all that water onto another lime and cook it until it becomes new again.
It will then be very strong caustic that is used in many medical procedures and in cauterizing other body parts. Because it produces the effect of fire itself.
And they are among the medicines with which the ancha is cauterized; also like tesisie, and wild honey, and lime mixed with soap so that both are combined.
And indeed Galen told about the treatment of an ancient man who was cured of pain in the hip and sciatic vein; and he praised it as being very effective. He said that he did not require any other treatment and was healed with a single application of the medicine until he reported that perhaps he entered a bath while carrying it, and left already healed.
And it is to be taken from green setaragi; and if you cannot find the green type then use a dry fresh one instead, grinding it with some fat and applying it to wherever there is pain in the hip, leg or thigh; bandaging it for three hours or as long as the patient can bear the burning sensation. Then place him in a bath.
When his body is damp, place him on a couch. For the pain goes away and he heals.
And you should know that no one should use an iron cauterizer with these medicines unless after the body has been evacuated.
And Dioscorides who said that goat dung, when it is used to cauterize the sciatic vein, benefits it; and it becomes a caustic agent in this way. Wool should be taken and soaked in old oil, then placed on the deep spot located between the big toe and the one next to it.
Then take dry goat dung and ignite it in the fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place [the charcoal] on top of the wool and leave it there until it is extinguished. Then repeat this process. Therefore, you should not cease doing this until sensation returns to the affected area via movement up to the groin, and the pain is alleviated.
And this manner of cautery is called the 'Goat Cautery'.
Concerning the cauterization for back pain.
At times, pain occurs in the back due to many causeseither by accident or impact, or due to superfluous evacuation (of bodily waste), and similar occurrences caused by an influx of cold and moist matter: and cauterization is not suitable except for this one type, which results from the influx of cold matter.
Therefore, after the patient's evacuation with foul-smelling pills or similar, three lines should be drawn across the back where there is pain according to the width of the patient's thumb, and once marked with encaustic [paint], five cauterizations (or more depending on the quantity that results from the tolerance of the patient's strength) are applied along each line; and this cauterization should be done using a cautery needle.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using a clavate central cautery, according to this form.
On the method of cauterization at the beginning of a hernia.
This illness often occurs in small children.
And the sign of its beginning in boys is: when it happens to him as a tightening with shortness of breath during exertion, and movement; and you find at the lower end of the spine and its knobs, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When you see it like this and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
And let the cautery cover all parts of the vertebra equally; and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a two or three-pronged cautery, and let the prongs be close to each other.
Then treat the area until it heals with what we have said.
And beware of using the cautery on a hernia that is caused by a spasm of nerve.
On the method of cauterization for podagra and joint pains.
When joint pains are caused by cold humidity that overflows to any part of the body, then when they happen to the feet, it is customary for doctors to call it podagra specifically.
When gout caused by cold is treated with the methods of cure and the pain does not go away, then the cautery removes it.
And it is necessary that you cauterize him after evacuation at the joints of the feet with many cauteries; and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to make a puncture over the surface of the foot, then use the dot-shaped cautery. If the pain rises up to the knees or other joints, and this happens frequently, then cauterize it over each knee with three cauteries, or four on every side, using the same Claw-shaped cautery.
But if more of this cautery is necessary, then cauterize it. And do not plunge your hand with the cautery, but let it be about as thick as the skin.
If the pain rises to the knees and back, then apply what we have said from the cautery in its chapter.

And you do not discharge the sick man from good regimen or from taking medicines. If a good diet is maintained and the phlegm is evacuated, healing will occur by God's help with this caustic.
On the method of cauterizing ruptures.
When there is a rupture in the groin and the intestine descends or the bag comes close to the testicle, then you should advise the patient to forgo food for that day. And he should take something laxative so that his stool descends from the belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back; and tell him to hold his breath until the bag or intestine comes out.
Next, bring it back with your fingers and mark it with caustic under the rupture on the pectineal bone, making a sign whose end is like half a circle towards the upper body.
Then use a fire to cauterize it with this shape until it becomes white and flakes fall off. Next bring the intestine or bag back to its cavity. Then let the assistant put his hand on that place so that the intestine does not come out: and you have opened between the patient's legs, placed a pillow underneath him, and one servant is on his legs, another on his chest holding his hands.
Next put the caustic on that mark with your hand held straight. And hold on to it until you reach the bone with it; or repeat with it a second time if you have not reached the bone with it the first time.
And observe with caution from the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and thereby upon the patient befall either death or great harm.
And know that when you do not achieve with the cauterization of the bone, your operation is not helpful.
And it should be that the cautery for infants is delicate, according to their measure.
Then take care with the other ointments until it heals.
And let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide nourishment for the duration of their treatment, which soothes their belly; so that the intestine does not leave during strain and defecation.
Then when they wish to rise after forty days, then apply a strap made poorly, and let them wear it for another forty days.
And they should be lessened from work, and fullness of food and drink, and loud voices.
For when one follows this regime, they heal with complete healing.
And I shall say the treatment of ruptures with incision in its own chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the rest of the belly, and they are beginning, and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize their rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and let what is burned be like one third of it. Then treat it with what we have said; and it will not increase.
And now some of the first [surgeons] said: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular shaped cautery like this.
After it is sealed with wax, and a line placed which runs across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with the pointed cautery.
But the first [method] is easier and better.
On the method of cauterization for pains caused by falling or being struck.
Chapter 48.
When there is pain in some limbs caused by falling or being struck and the pain persists over a long period of time without healing with medicines, then it should be treated with the pointed cautery.
And the size of the cautery should be appropriate for each limb, taking into account its size, weakness and strength, as well as the location of any twisting or pain.
If it therefore heals with the first [treatment], that is good. If not, then repeat on the same spot.
For it is customary of these pains to move from the limb to that which is closest to it. Which is why you must follow them with the cautery until the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterization for leprosy.
Leprous people sometimes benefit from being cauterized greatly. And especially the type of leprosy, which arises due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy; when you wish to cauterize it, therefore consider this.
If therefore the leprosy is in its beginning stages and you have treated it with what we said earlier in our division but it has not descended or stopped; and you are afraid that corruption will overcome his entire constitution: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the scalp, and a second below this towards the front near the end of the hairline, and two on each temple area, and one behind on the back of the neck.
And finally hold your hand with the cautery there briefly until it imprints a small impression on the bone and some of its layers are dislocated so that you alleviate the exhalation of thick vapors from him; and cauterize also over his spleen, as we mentioned previously.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the afflicted and is clearly apparent then it behooves you to cauterize him with those same cauteries which we mentioned for the head; and also a cautery on the tip of his nose, and two cauteries over both jawbones, and two cauteries over the vertebrae of his neck, and six over the vertebrae of his back, and one large one on his coccyx (tailbone) and one above it in the gluteal area; and two over each hip: that is to say one over each hip bone and two over both knees: one over each knee and two over his shoulders, and two over his elbows, and two over the tenderness of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from among all of the finger joints of his hands and feet; and cauterize also over all the heel bones in his feet and the palms of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the back of the heel, so as not to burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with one cautery over the breastbone, and another over the stomach, and another over the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater the benefit and the more effective it is.
And know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body has already become numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of different sizes and widths according to the limbs and joints, just as was stated previously regarding the types of tools.
Then treat the cautery with a paste of herb flour mixed with honey, and continue with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for stupor (loss of sensation).
When any limb becomes numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but does not heal, then cauterize the affected numb limb with cauteries according to the size or smallness of that limb.
Let your cautery penetrate into the thickness of the skin just slightly. Then treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a type of numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, at the vertebrae of the back near where the nerves emerge which move that limb; and the numbness is removed.
Indeed, one must not presume to do so unless they are wise in the anatomy of members and the emergence of nerves that move the body.
Chapter 51.
When you treat Albaras and do not add anything to it from the art of medicine: then cauterize over it with a deep cauterization to some extent, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its colour changes.
Then treat it with a mixture of herb flour and lentil flour with rose oil, arnica leaves, pigeon blood, and swallow blood: let there be one part of each; mix all these together, lay them on a cloth, and attach this to the place until it is healed.
On the method of cauterization for cancer.
When cancer is starting, and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cauterization around its circumference, as it revolves.
The wise have said that one should cauterize with the final cauterization in its middle.
That does not seem right to me, for I fear that it may ulcerate; and indeed I have seen this happen several times.
And it is better that one be cauterized around its circumference with a circle, as we said; or with multiple cauterizations.
On the method of cauterization for adobelatis.
When someone has a swelling that is slow to mature, either due to the excess of humours causing it or because of the age of the patient who has little blood and is decrepit, or because of time constraints, and you need to hurry up the maturation of the swelling, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it alone. For itself will hurry up with the maturation.
But if you want to perforate it with the cautery then heat up a cautery that is of this shape: [shape inserted in original prompt]
And place it in the middle of the swelling until it penetrates the skin and let the patient be treated with what follows to alleviate the course of purity.
Then treat it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing an ulcerating sore.
Chapter 54.
An ulcerating sore is nothing other than a corruption walking on the limb and consuming it like fire eats dry wood.
If you see an ulcerating sore in a place that can tolerate being burnt with fire then burn it with many fires, small and large nails, according to what is appropriate for the location of the ulcer.
Then burn it from all sides until you uproot the entire corruption so that nothing of it remains whatsoever.
Then leave it alone for three days and put ground sulphur mixed with oil on the places that have been burnt until all scabs and corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with flesh-generating salves.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh is born of healthy constitution, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery on that which remains of the corrupted areas.
And corrosive medicines are sometimes treated with sharp medicine. For it arises in the place of the cautery.
However, the cautery with fire is of swifter aid: and indeed I have already said its cauterization with sharp medicine in the division: so take it there when you need it.
On the method of cauterizing in claws and warts.
Section 55.
Many times this illness occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, filtered thing that harms the foot.
And indeed the cautery on them is according to two methods: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As much as it is with fire, make the cautery bowl similar to an eagle's feather: which shall be made of iron, according to the size that contains a nail on every side: and let it be thin at the edges.
Then place it burning over the claw. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the claw, until you reach the depth of the claw: and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply plasters made with crushed mulberries, mixed with salt; leave the plaster on overnight. It will be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the place with an emollient for newborn skin until it heals.
If they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on hands and feet: then apply a hot iron cauterization to them; take a copper, iron or vulture feather pipe and place it over a nail or charcoal ember. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the pipe; hold your hand and rotate it with finger pressure for a while so that the edge of the pipe touches the root of the nail, allowing the hot water to reach deep down to the root of the nail: have the patient wait a little over the hot-water cauterization for about an hour.
Then leave it be, for the nail will be eradicated along with its roots.
Do this to each one after another until you have treated all of them on the body.
Then treat them after they are eradicated with something that generates flesh from ointments.
On the method of tremor cauterization:
When someone has a tremor from cold nerve damage or from quartan fever or some other cause: then you should cauterize them with four to five hot iron probes over the vertebrae and between each vertebra with one probe; on their chest with another, and over their stomach with yet another.
For tremors are calmed with olive oil cauterization, and healing is hastened for ailments that are cold.
In the way of cauterization by Albucasis.
Chapter 57.
Sometimes bad humours, that is boils, are expelled from the body which arise from corrupted gross matter.
Therefore it is necessary that when they first appear, the boils should be cauterised over their entire head with a fine myrtle wood stick whose end has been lit by fire. Or with the root of long aristolochia. Or with a bean-shaped iron cauterizer.
And sometimes they are cauterised at the beginning of their formation in this way: and they do not increase: and the superfluity that makes them is broken apart, and they are cured of it.
However it must be done after evacuation by bloodletting.
On the way of cauterization for bleeding from an artery into a wound.
It often happens that there is bleeding from an artery which has been cut at a wound, which occurs externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or member cauterization, and similar to these: and it becomes difficult to stop it.
So when it happens to someone, then quickly place your hand over the artery opening, and put your index finger on top of it: and squeeze it a lot, until the blood is blocked underneath your finger, and nothing comes out from it.
Then place on the fire small olive oil-based cauteries and several large ones; blow upon them until they become very hot.
Then take one of these, small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery has been severed, and apply the cautery to the vein; then remove your finger quickly and hold the cautery in position until the bleeding stops.
If it is expelled as you raise your finger from the artery opening and the cautery goes out, then quickly take another cautery from those already prepared on the fire.
Therefore do not stop applying one after another until the bleeding stops.
And be careful not to burn the nerve that is there, lest another evil happen to the patient.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, it is not possible to stop it unless by one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or by extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is extracted, its ends contract and the bleeding stops. Or it may be tied with a strong ligature. Or place on it some medicines which have the property of stopping blood, and bind it with a suitable compress.
He who accomplishes the stopping of blood by means of a ligament and a compress, or by the application of burning substances and the like, should never apply them to him completely except rarely.
If it happens to someone and there is no doctor present nor medicine: then begin with the placement of the index finger on the vein's opening, as we described, and its strong compression until the blood is blocked from the upper part of the wound and above the artery. And the finger should not be removed from it but placed above with very cold water until the blood clots and thickens, then cut off.
And meanwhile consider what it requires from cauterization or medicine.
On incision, perforation, and bloodletting with regard to wounds and similar issues.
We have already spoken in the first chapter about every illness that requires a burning cautery and medicinal fire, along with its opportunities, causes, instruments, and types of cauterization.
